2
07/12/2025
2Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-3Introduction
• The design of the imperative languages is 
based directly on the von Neumann 
architecture
– Efficiency is the primary concern, rather than 
the suitability of the language for software 
development
• The design of the functional languages is 
based on mathematical functions
– A solid theoretical basis that is also closer to the 
user, but relatively unconcerned with the 
architecture of the machines on which programs 
will run
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-4Mathematical Functions
• A mathematical function is a mapping of 
members of one set, called the domain set , 
to another set, called the range set
• A lambda expression specifies the 
parameter(s) and the mapping of a function 
in the following form
(x) x * x * x
for the function  cube(x) = x * x * x3
4
07/12/2025
3Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-5Lambda Expressions
• Lambda expressions describe nameless 
functions
• Lambda expressions are applied to 
parameter(s) by placing the parameter(s) 
after the expression
e.g.,   ((x) x * x * x)(2)
which evaluates to 8
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-6Functional Forms
• A higher-order function, or functional 
form, is one that either takes functions as 
parameters or yields a function as its result, 
or both5
6
07/12/2025
4Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-7Function Composition
• A functional form that takes two functions 
as parameters and yields a function whose 
value is the first actual parameter function 
applied to the application of the second
Form: h f °g
which means h (x) f ( g ( x))
For f (x) x + 2and  g (x) 3 * x,
h f °gyields (3 * x)+ 2
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-8Apply-to-all
• A functional form that takes a single 
function as a parameter and yields a list of 
values obtained by applying the given 
function to each element of a list of 
parameters
Form: 
For h(x) x * x
(h, (2, 3, 4)) yields  (4, 9, 16)7
8
07/12/2025
5Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-9Fundamentals of Functional 
Programming Languages
• The objective of the design of a FPL is to mimic 
mathematical functions to the greatest extent possible
• The basic process of computation is fundamentally 
different in a FPL than in an imperative language
– In an imperative language, operations are done and the 
results are stored in variables for later use
– Management of variables is a constant concern and 
source of complexity for imperative programming
• In an FPL, variables are not necessary, as is the case in 
mathematics
•Referential Transparency - In an FPL, the evaluation of a 
function always produces the same result given the 
same parameters
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-10Lisp Data Types and Structures
•Data object types : originally only atoms and 
lists
•List form : parenthesized collections of 
sublists and/or atoms
e.g., (A B (C D) E)
• Originally, Lisp was a typeless language
• Lisp lists are stored internally as single-
linked lists9
10
07/12/2025
6Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-11Lisp Interpretation
• Lambda notation is used to specify functions and 
function definitions. Function applications and data 
have the same form.
e.g., If the list (A B C) is interpreted as data it is
a simple list of three atoms, A, B, and C
If it is interpreted as a function application,
it means that the function named Ais
applied to the two parameters, Band C
• The first Lisp interpreter appeared only as a  
demonstration of the universality of the 
computational capabilities of the notation
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-12Origins of Scheme
• A mid-1970s dialect of Lisp, designed to 
be a cleaner, more modern, and simpler 
version than the contemporary dialects of 
Lisp
• Uses only static scoping
• Functions are first-class entities
– They can be the values of expressions and 
elements of lists
– They can be assigned to variables, passed as 
parameters, and returned from functions11
12
07/12/2025
7The Scheme Interpreter
• In interactive mode, the Scheme interpreter 
is an infinite read-evaluate-print loop 
(REPL)
– This form of interpreter is also used by Python 
and Ruby
• Expressions are interpreted by the function 
EVAL
• Literals evaluate to themselves
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-13
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-14Primitive Function Evaluation
• Parameters are evaluated, in no particular 
order
• The values of the parameters are 
substituted into the function body
• The function body is evaluated
• The value of the last expression in the 
body is the value of the function13
14
07/12/2025
8Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-15Primitive Functions & LAMBDAExpressions
• Primitive Arithmetic Functions: +, -, *, /, ABS, SQRT, 
REMAINDER , MIN, MAX
e.g., (+ 5 2) yields 7
• Lambda Expressions
– Form is based on notation
e.g., (LAMBDA (x) (* x x))
xis called a bound variable
• Lambda expressions can be applied to parameters
e.g., ((LAMBDA (x) (* x x)) 7)
• LAMBDA expressions can have any number of parameters
(LAMBDA (a b x) (+ (* a x x) (* b x)))
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-16Special Form Function: DEFINE
• DEFINE - Two forms:
1. To bind a symbol to an expression
e.g., (DEFINE pi 3.141593)
Example use: (DEFINE two_pi (* 2 pi))
These symbols are not variables – they are like the names 
bound by Java’s finaldeclarations
2. To bind names to lambda expressions ( LAMBDAis 
implicit)
e.g., (DEFINE (square x) (* x x))
Example use: (square 5)
-The evaluation process for DEFINE is different! The first 
parameter is never evaluated. The second parameter is 
evaluated and bound to the first parameter. 15
16
07/12/2025
9Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-17Output Functions
• Usually not needed, because the interpreter 
always displays the result of a function 
evaluated at the top level (not nested)
• Scheme has PRINTF, which is similar to the 
printffunction of C
• Note: explicit input and output are not part 
of the pure functional programming model, 
because input operations change the state 
of the program and output operations are 
side effects
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-18Numeric Predicate Functions
• #T(or #t) is true and #F(or #f) is false 
(sometimes ()is used for false)
• =, <>, >, <, >=, <=
• EVEN?, ODD?, ZERO?, NEGATIVE?
• The NOTfunction inverts the logic of a 
Boolean expression17
18
07/12/2025
10Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-19Control Flow
• Selection- the special form, IF
(IFpredicate then_exp else_exp )
(IF (<> count 0)
(/ sum count)
)
• Recall from Chapter 8 the CONDfunction:
(DEFINE (leap? year)
(COND
((ZERO? (MODULO year 400)) #T)
((ZERO? (MODULO year 100)) #F)
(ELSE (ZERO? (MODULO year 4)))
))
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-20List Functions
• QUOTE -takes one parameter; returns the 
parameter without evaluation
– QUOTE is required because the Scheme interpreter, 
named EVAL, always evaluates parameters to function 
applications before applying the function.  QUOTEis 
used to avoid parameter evaluation when it is not 
appropriate
– QUOTE can be abbreviated with the apostrophe prefix 
operator
'(A B)is equivalent to (QUOTE (A B))
• Recall that CAR, CDR, and CONSwere covered in 
Chapter 619
20
07/12/2025
11Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-21List Functions (continued)
• Examples:
(CAR ′((A B) C D)) returns (A B)
(CAR ′A) is an error
(CDR ′((A B) C D)) returns (C D)
(CDR ′A) is an error
(CDR ′(A)) returns ()
(CONS ′() ′(A B)) returns (() A B)
(CONS ′(A B) ′(C D)) returns ((A B) C D)
(CONS ′A ′B) returns (A . B)(a dotted pair )
List Functions (continued)
• LISTis a function for building a list from 
any number of parameters
(LIST ′apple ′orange ′grape) returns
(apple orange grape)
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-2221
22
07/12/2025
12Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-23Predicate Function: EQ?
• EQ?takes two expressions as parameters 
(usually two atoms); it returns #Tif both 
parameters have the same pointer value; 
otherwise #F
(EQ? 'A 'A) yields #T
(EQ? 'A 'B) yields#F
(EQ? 'A '(A B)) yields #F
(EQ? '(A B) '(A B)) yields #Tor #F
(EQ? 3.4 (+ 3 0.4))) yields#Tor#F
Predicate Function: EQV?
• EQV?is like EQ?, except that it works for both 
symbolic and numeric atoms; it is a value 
comparison, not a pointer comparison
(EQV? 3 3) yields#T
(EQV? 'A 3) yields #F
(EQV 3.4 (+ 3 0.4)) yields #T
(EQV? 3.0 3) yields #F (floats and integers are 
different)
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-2423
24
07/12/2025
13Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-25Predicate Functions: LIST?and NULL?
• LIST?takes one parameter; it returns #Tif the 
parameter is a list; otherwise #F
(LIST? '()) yields #T
• NULL?takes one parameter; it returns #Tif the 
parameter is the empty list; otherwise #F
(NULL? '(())) yields #F
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-26Example Scheme Function: member
• member takes an atom and a simple list; 
returns #Tif the atom is in the list; #F
otherwise
DEFINE (member atm a_list)
(COND
((NULL? a_list) #F)
((EQ? atm (CAR a_list)) #T)
((ELSE (member atm (CDR a_list)))
))25
26
07/12/2025
14Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-27Example Scheme Function: equalsimp
• equalsimp takes two simple lists as parameters; 
returns #Tif the two simple lists are equal; #F
otherwise
(DEFINE (equalsimp list1 list2)
(COND
((NULL? list1) (NULL? list2))
((NULL? list2) #F)
((EQ? (CAR list1) (CAR list2))
(equalsimp(CDR list1)(CDR list2)))
(ELSE #F)
))
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-28Example Scheme Function: equal
• equal takes two general lists as parameters;  
returns #Tif the two lists are equal; #F otherwise
(DEFINE (equal list1 list2)
(COND
((NOT (LIST? list1))(EQ? list1 list2))
((NOT (LIST? list2)) #F)
((NULL? list1) (NULL? list2))
((NULL? list2) #F)
((equal (CAR list1) (CAR list2))
(equal (CDR list1) (CDR list2)))
(ELSE #F)
))27
28
07/12/2025
15Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-29Example Scheme Function: append
• append takes two lists as parameters; returns the 
first parameter list with the elements of the second 
parameter list appended at the end
(DEFINE (append list1 list2)
(COND
((NULL? list1) list2)
(ELSE (CONS (CAR list1)
(append (CDR list1) list2)))
))
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-30Example Scheme Function: LET
• Recall that LETwas discussed in Chapter 5
• LETis actually shorthand for a LAMBDA
expression applied to a parameter
(LET ((alpha 7))(* 5 alpha))
is the same as:
((LAMBDA (alpha) (* 5 alpha)) 7)29

07/12/2025
16Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-31LETExample
(DEFINE (quadratic_roots a b c)
(LET (
(root_part_over_2a 
(/ (SQRT (- (* b b) (* 4 a c)))(* 2 a)))
(minus_b_over_2a (/ (- 0 b) (* 2 a)))
(LIST (+ minus_b_over_2a root_part_over_2a))
(- minus_b_over_2a root_part_over_2a))
))
Tail Recursion in Scheme
• Definition: A function is tail recursive if its 
recursive call is the last operation in the 
function
• A tail recursive function can be 
automatically converted by a compiler to 
use iteration, making it faster
• Scheme language definition requires that 
Scheme language systems convert all tail 
recursive functions to use iteration
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-3231
32
07/12/2025
17Tail Recursion in Scheme - continued
• Example of rewriting a function to make it 
tail recursive, using helper a function
Original: (DEFINE (factorial n)
(IF (<= n 0)
1
(* n (factorial (- n 1)))
))
Tail recursive: (DEFINE (facthelper n factpartial)
(IF (<= n 0)
factpartial
(facthelper(- n 1) (* n factpartial)))
)
(DEFINE (factorial n)
(facthelper n 1))
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-33
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-34Functional Form - Composition
• Composition
– If his the composition of fand g, h(x) = f(g(x))
(DEFINE (g x) (* 3 x))
(DEFINE (f x) (+ 2 x))
(DEFINE h x) (+ 2 (* 3 x))) (The composition)
– In Scheme, the functional composition function compose
can be written:
(DEFINE (compose f g) (LAMBDA (x) (f (g x))))
((compose CAR CDR) '((a b) c d)) yields c
(DEFINE (third a_list)
((compose CAR (compose CDR CDR)) a_list))33
34
07/12/2025
18Functional Form – Apply-to-All
• Apply to All - one form in Scheme is map
– Applies the given function to all elements of the given list; 
(DEFINE (map fun a_list)
(COND
((NULL? a_list) '())
(ELSE (CONS (fun (CAR a_list))
(map fun (CDR a_list))))
))
(map (LAMBDA (num) (* num num num)) '(3 4 2 6)) yields
(27 64 8 216)
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-35
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-36Functions That Build Code
• It is possible in Scheme to define a function 
that builds Scheme code and requests its 
interpretation
• This is possible because the interpreter is a 
user-available function, EVAL35

19Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-37Adding a List of Numbers
((DEFINE (adder a_list)
(COND
((NULL? a_list) 0)
(ELSE (EVAL (CONS '+ a_list)))
))
• The parameter is a list of numbers to be added; 
adderinserts a +operator and evaluates the 
resulting list
– Use CONSto insert the atom +into the list of numbers.
– Be sure that +is quoted to prevent evaluation
– Submit the new list to EVALfor evaluation
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-38Common Lisp
• A combination of many of the features of the 
popular dialects of Lisp around in the early 1980s
• A large and complex language--the opposite of 
Scheme
• Features include:
– records 
– arrays 
– complex numbers
– character strings
– powerful I/O capabilities
– packages with access control
– iterative control statements37
38
07/12/2025
20Common Lisp (continued)
• Macros
– Create their effect in two steps:
•Expand the macro
•Evaluate the expanded macro
• Some of the predefined functions of 
Common Lisp are actually macros
• Users can define their own macros with 
DEFMACRO
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-39
Common Lisp (continued)
• Backquote operator ( `)
– Similar to the Scheme’s QUOTE, except that some 
parts of the parameter can be unquoted by 
preceding them with commas
`(a (* 3 4) c) evaluates to (a (* 3 4) c)
`(a ,(* 3 4) c) evaluates to (a 12 c)
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-4039
40
07/12/2025
21Common Lisp (continued)
• Reader Macros
– Lisp implementations have a front end called the reader
that transforms Lisp into a code representation. Then 
macro calls are expanded into the code representation. 
– A reader macro is a special kind of macro that is 
expanded during the reader phase
– A reader macro is a definition of a single character, which 
is expanded into its Lisp definition
– An example of a reader macro is an apostrophe character, 
which is expanded into a call to QUOTE
– Users can define their own reader macros as a kind of 
shorthand
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-41
Common Lisp (continued)
• Common Lisp has a symbol data type 
(similar to that of Ruby)
– The reserved words are symbols that evaluate to 
themselves
– Symbols are either bound or unbound
•Parameter symbols are bound while the function is 
being evaluated
•Symbols that are the names of imperative style 
variables that have been assigned values are bound
•All other symbols are unbound
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-4241
42
07/12/2025
22Common Lisp (continued)
; :foo is a keyword symbol — evaluates to itself
:foo  ; => :FOO
; Define a function with a parameter symbol 'x'
(defun square (x)
(* x x))
(square 4) ; => 16 (x is bound to 4 during call)
; Assign a variable 'a'
(setf a 5)
a ; => 5 (bound symbol)
; Try to evaluate an unbound symbol 'b'
b ; => Error: The variable B is unbound.
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-43
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-44Support for Functional Programming in 
Primarily Imperative Languages
• Support for functional programming is 
increasingly creeping into imperative 
languages
– Anonymous functions (lambda expressions)
•JavaScript: leave the name out of a function 
definition
•C#: i => (i % 2) == 0 (returns true or false 
depending on whether the parameter is even or 
odd)
•Python: lambda a, b : 2 * a  - b43
44
07/12/2025
23Support for Functional Programming in 
Primarily Imperative Languages (continued)
• Python supports the higher-order functions filter 
and map (often use lambda expressions as their 
first parameters)
map(lambda x : x ** 3, [2, 4, 6, 8])
Returns [8, 64, 216, 512]
• Python supports partial function applications
fromoperator import add
add5 = partial (add, 5)
(the first line imports add as a function)
Use: add5(15)
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-45
Support for Functional Programming in 
Primarily Imperative Languages (continued)
• Ruby Blocks
– Are effectively subprograms that are sent to 
methods, which makes the method a higher-
order subprogram
– A block can be converted to a subprogram 
object with lambda
times = lambda {|a, b| a * b}
Use: x = times.(3, 4) (sets xto 12)
– Times can be curried with
times5 = times.curry.(5)
Use: x5 = times5.(3) (sets x5to 15)
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-4645
46
07/12/2025
24Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-47Comparing Functional and Imperative 
Languages
• Imperative Languages:
– Efficient execution
– Complex semantics
– Complex syntax
– Concurrency is programmer designed
• Functional Languages:
– Simple semantics
– Simple syntax
– Less efficient execution
– Programs can automatically be made concurrent 
Copyright © 2018 Pearson. All rights reserved. 1-48Summary
• Functional programming languages use function application, 
conditional expressions, recursion, and functional forms to 
control program execution
• Lisp began as a purely functional language and later included 
imperative features
• Scheme is a relatively simple dialect of Lisp that uses static 
scoping exclusively
• Common Lisp is a large Lisp-based language
• ML is a static-scoped and strongly typed functional language 
that uses type inference
• Haskell is a lazy functional language supporting infinite lists 
and set comprehension.
• F# is a .NET functional language that also supports 
imperative and object-oriented programming
• Some primarily imperative languages now incorporate some 
support for functional programming
• Purely functional languages have advantages over imperative 
alternatives, but still are not very widely used47
48

 لوﻷا لاؤسلا   4 درجات  Grades 4  Question  1 
اذكر أربعة  معايير أساسية لتقييم اللغات مدختسُت  ﻓﻲ 
تصميم لغات البرمجة، واشرحها بإيجاز. لكل معيار، 
 ِطعأ  ًﻻاﺛم للغة برمجية تحقﻖ درجة عالية وأخرى  ضعيفة 
ﻓي هذا  المعيار، مﻊ توضيح السبب.  List and brieﬂy explain four primary language 
evaluation criteria used in programming-
language design . For each criterion, give one 
example of a language that scores highly and 
one that scores poorly on that criterion, 
explaining why. 
1. Readability  
Explanation:  
Readability measures how easily code written in the language can be understood by humans. 
Factors include clarity, syntax simplicity, and consistency. 
 High: Python 
Python emphasizes clear, readable syntax with indentation-based blocks and 
minimal punctuation, making it easy for beginners and experienced programmers to 
understand code quickly. 
 Low: Perl 
Perl’s syntax is often short and includes many symbols and shortcuts, which can 
make it hard to read and understand, especially for new programmers. 
 
2. Writability 
Explanation:  
Writability assesses how easily programmers can express ideas in the language. This includes 
the expressiveness of the syntax and the availability of powerful abstractions. 
 High: Ruby 
Ruby oƯers expressive syntax and elegant features like blocks, mixins, and meta -
programming, allowing programmers to write concise and natural code. 
 Low: Assembly Language  
Assembly is very low-level with verbose, cumbersome instructions, making it hard to 
write high-level abstractions or express complex logic succinctly. 
 
3. Reliability 
Explanation:  
Reliability evaluates how well the language prevents bugs and runtime errors, including strong 
typing, error checking, and safe memory management. 
 High: Haskell 
Haskell’s strong static type system and pure functional nature catch many errors at 
compile time, increasing reliability signiﬁcantly. 
 Low: C 
C allows direct memory manipulation with pointers and lacks automatic memory 
management, which often leads to undeﬁned behavior and bugs like bu Ưer overﬂows.  
 
4. Cost 
Explanation:  
Cost refers to the overall expenses associated with using the language, including licensing 
fees, development time, and maintenance costs. 
 High (Low Cost):  JavaScript  
JavaScript is free, widely supported, and has a vast ecosystem, making development 
and deployment low cost. It runs in all modern browsers without extra licensing fees, 
reducing infrastructure and support expenses. 
 Low (High Cost): C++  
While C++ itself is free and open-source, the cost of development with C++ can be 
high due to longer development times, the complexity of the language, need for 
specialized expertise, and extensive testing requirements, leading to increased labor 
costs compared  to higher-level languages.

التي يتم التحكم ﻓيها ؟اًيقطنم  What are design issues for logically 
controlled loop statements? 
 
The main design issues with logically controlled loops are:  
– Pretest or posttest? 
This issue concerns the test of the loop should be at the beginning of the loop such as 
a while statement or at the end of the loop such as do while statements. 
 
– Should the logically controlled loop be a special case of the counting loop statement 
or a separate statement?  
 
– Complexity and Side E Ưects in Loop Conditions  
Complex conditions with pointers and assignment statements can cause side e Ưects 
that make loops harder to follow,

  B();

السؤال الرابع  4 درجات  Grades 4  Question 4  
      
اكتب مناقشة قصيرة حول ما ﻓقدناه وما اكتسبناه ﻓي قرار 
مصممي Java بعدم تضمين مؤشرات C .++  Write a short discussion of what was lost and 
what was gained in Java’s designers’ decision 
to not include the pointers of C++. 
 
Discussion on Java's Exclusion of Pointers (Compared to C++):  
What was lost:  
 Fine-grained memory control:  Programmers cannot directly 
manipulate memory addresses or perform pointer arithmetic, which 
limits low-level system programming and can reduce opportunities for 
certain performance optimizations. 
 Flexibility and power:  Features like custom memory management, 
manual object layout, and complex data structure manipulations that 
rely on pointer arithmetic are not possible. 
 Compatibility with existing C/C++ code:  Direct porting or interfacing 
with pointer-heavy code is more difficult. 
What was gained:  
 Improved safety and security:  Java eliminates a major source of 
bugs like dangling pointers, buffer overflows, and memory corruption 
by disallowing direct memory access. This helps prevent many 
common security vulnerabilities. 
 Simplified programming model:  Developers avoid complex and 
error-prone pointer arithmetic, making code easier to write, read, and 
maintain—particularly beneficial for beginners. 
 Enhanced portability:  By abstracting memory management, Java 
programs run consistently across different platforms without concern 
for hardware-specific memory layout. 
 Automatic memory management:  Java relies on a garbage collector 
to manage memory, reducing programmer overhead and the risk of 
memory leaks common in pointer-intensive code.

Question 2:                                          4 Marks السؤال  مقر 2                             :4  تاجرد  
Consider the following code snippet, which 
uses pass-by-reference and has nested 
subprograms. 
   يذلا ،ﻲلاتلا دوكلا فطتقم رابتعﻻا ﻲﻓ ذخأنل
  جمارب ىلع يوتحيو عجرملا ربع ليوحتلا مدختسي
ﻓرعية متداخلة. 
(Pascal) 
program Main; 
var x : integer; 
 
procedure A(var m : integer); 
    procedure B(var n : integer); 
    begin 
        n := n + 10; 
        x := n - 5; 
    end; { B } 
 
begin { A } 
    B(m); 
end; { A } 
 
begin { Main } 
    x := 10; 
    A(x); 
    writeln(x); 
end. { Main } 
```   
a) Assuming static scoping, what value is 
printed by the `writeln(x)` statement in 
the Main program? Trace the execution 
step-by-step, showing the values of `x` 
and the parameters `m` and `n` to 
justify your answer. أ-    ﻲتلا ةميقلا ﻲه ام ،تباثلا ديدحتلا ضارتﻓاب
تطبعها عبارة 'writeln(x)'   جمانربلا ﻲﻓ
  عم ،ةوطخب ةوطخ ذيفنتلا عبتت ؟ﻲسيئرلا
عرض قيم 'x'  والمعلمات'm'   و'n'   ريربتل
إجابتك.  
Answer: 
Because the passing of parameters is by reference, all formal parameters get a reference to 
the actual parameter (that is, the formal parameter variable and the actual parameter point to 
the same area in memory).  
In the code we obser ve that x is a global variable therefore it is common to all the program. In 
the main program calls the subprogram A(x), x is passed by reference therefore, the formal 
parameter m is linked to the same memory location as x and any changes made to m reﬂect 
directly on x. The same principle applies when A calls B passing m as an argument to the 
formal parameter n. Therefore, x, m, and n share the same memory location.    
In B    
        n=n+10 = 10+10 =20    x=20    m=20    
        x=x-5 =20-5=15        n=15    m=15    
Result the program pr ints 15   
   
b) Explain the role of the Static Link  in the 
activation record for procedure `B` 
when it is called from procedure `A`. To 
which activation record does the Static 
Link in `B`'s activation record point?  ب-  اشرح دور الرابط الثابت  ﻓ   ليعفتلا لجس ﻲ
لﻺجراء 'B'   ءارجﻹا نم هؤاعدتسا متي امدنع
'A'.   تباثلا طبارلا ريشي ليعفت لجس يأ ىلإ
ﻓﻲ سجل التفعيل الخاص ب 'B' ؟  
    رقم القي____________________________:اسم الطالب  _______________:د  
   
The static link is a pointer (or reference) included in the activation record of a procedure that 
points to the activation record of the enclosing procedure in which the current procedure was 
deﬁned. 
In this program, B is nested inside  A, so under static scoping : 
The Static Link  in B’s activation record points to the activation record of its enclosing 
procedure , which is A.  
Question 3:                                         6   Marks  السؤال رقم3                               6  
درجات  
Analyze the following C++ code.   حلل جمانربلا التالﻲ ب C++.  
#include <iostream>  
using namespace std; 
class Base { 
public: 
    virtual void display() { 
        cout << "Inside Base::display()" << endl; 
    } 
    void print() { 
        cout << "Inside Base::print()" << endl; 
    } 
}; 
class Derived : public Base { 
public: 
    void display() override { 
        cout << "Inside Derived::display()" << 
endl; 
    } 
    void print() { 
        cout << "Inside Derived::print()" << endl; 
    } 
}; 
int main() { 
    Base* basePtr; 
    Derived derivedObj; 
    basePtr = &derivedObj; 
    // Call #1 
    basePtr->display(); 
    // Call #2 
    basePtr->print(); 
    return 0; 
} 
   
a) What is the output of Call #1 (`basePtr -
>display();`)? Explain why, using the 
correct terminology (e.g., virtual 
function, dynamic binding). أ-    تاجرخم وه ام Call #1 ('basePtr -
>display();'))   مادختساب ببسلا حرشا ؟
  ةحيحصلا تاحلطصملا) مثل الدالة 
اﻻﻓتراﺿية، الربط الديناميكﻲ( .  
Call #1 outputs:  
                       Inside Derived::display() 
Explanation: 
 Base::display() is declared virtual, so it is a virtual function . 
 basePtr is a pointer of type  Base* but it actually points to a  Derived object 
(derivedObj). 
 With virtual functions, C++ uses dynamic binding  (runtime polymorphism): at 
runtime, it looks at the dynamic type  of the object (Derived), not the static type of the 
pointer (Base*). 
 Therefore, the overridden method Derived::display() is called, producing the output 
above. 
 
b) What is the output of Call #2 (`basePtr -
>print();`)? Explain why its behavior is 
diƯerent from Call #1.   ب-    تاجرخم وه ام Call #2 ('basePtr -
>print();'))   نع فلتخي هكولس اذامل حرشا ؟
Call #1.  
Call #2 outputs:  
                     Inside Base::print() 
Explanation: 
 print() in Base is not declared virtual. 
 Even though Derived also deﬁnes a print() with the same name and signature, this is 
just name hiding , not overriding in the polymorphic sense. 
 For non-virtual functions, C++ uses static binding  (compile-time binding): the 
function to call is chosen based on the static type  of the pointer, which is Base*. 
 Therefore, basePtr->print() calls Base::print(), not Derived::print(), unlike display(), 
which is virtual and uses dynamic binding. 
 
   
c) If we changed the type of `basePtr` from 
`Base*` to `Derived*`, what would be 
the output of the two calls? Explain 
brieﬂy.  ت-  إذا غيرنا نوع 'basePtr ' نم ' Base  ىلإ '*
'Derived   ؟نيتملاكملا جرخم وه ام ،'*
 .راصتخاب حرشا  
  
If basePtr is changed to type  Derived* : 
Call #1 outputs:  
                       Inside Derived::display() 
Call #2 outputs:  
                     Inside Derived::print()  
Explanation (brief):  
 Call #1: display() is virtual and overridden in Derived, and the object is Derived, 
so Derived::display() is called. 
 Call #2: print() is non-virtual, but now the static type  of the pointer is Derived*, so the 
compiler binds the call to Derived::print() at compile time.

property related to the evaluation of 
expressions is referential transparency . 
An expression is referentially transparent 
if: 
a. It modiﬁes the state of variables 
outside its scope. 
b. It always produces the same 
result given the same inputs and 
has no side e Ưects. 
c. Its evaluation order can vary 
depending on compiler 
optimizations. 
d. It can be used as a parameter to 
another function. 
5.  Which of the following statements most

 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ3  من9     Page 3 of 9  السؤال الثاني  8 درجات  8 Marks Question 2  
رّﻓوُت لغﺎت البرمجﺔ  ًﻰنب متنوعﺔ  لﻼختيﺎر متعدد  
اﻻتجﺎهﺎت )مثل عبﺎرة switch ﻓي لغتي C/Java، 
وعبﺎرة case ﻓي لغتي Ada/Pascal، وسﻼسل elif  
ﻓي لغﺔ Python.(  
  
نﺎقش أربع قضﺎيﺎ تﺻميميﺔ مهمﺔ علﻰ  اﻷقل لعبﺎرات  
اﻻختيﺎر متعدد اﻻتجﺎهﺎت.   Programming languages o Ưer various 
constructs for multi-way selection (e.g., 
switch in C/Java, case in Ada/Pascal, elif 
chains in Python). 
 
Discuss at least four important design issues 
for multi-way selection statements.  
 
1. The Type of the Controlling Expression 
The ﬁrst major decision is what data types the "selector" variable can be. 
In early versions of C, the expression had to evaluate to an integer type. This allowed 
compilers to create highly e Ưicient "jump tables."  
Languages like Java and C# expanded this to include Strings and Enums. Python’s match 
statement (introduced in version 3.10) goes even further, allowing for complex object patterns 
and sequences. 
 
2. Speciﬁcation of Case Labels  
How ﬂexible should the labels be? Designers must decide if a case can only represent a 
single value or something broader. 
In standard C, each case is a single constant. Languages like Ada or Pascal allow for ranges 
(e.g., case 1..10:) or discrete lists (e.g., case 1, 3, 5:). 
 
3. Control Flow and "Fall-Through"  
What happens after the code for a speciﬁc case ﬁnish executing? 
In C, C++, and Java, execution "falls through" to the next case unless you explicitly use a 
break statement. This is often cited as a major source of bugs because programmers 
frequently forget the break. 
In Pascal, Ada, and Python, only the code for the matched case is executed, and control then 
exits the structure automatically. 
 
4. Exhaustiveness and Default Cases  
What should happen if the controlling expression doesn't match any of the provided case 
labels? 
Most languages provide a default or else branch. 
In some functional languages (like Haskell or Swift for enums), the compiler will throw an 
error if you haven't covered every possible value of the controlling expression. This ensures 
"type safety" and prevents unhandled edge cases. 
In older languages, if no case matches and there is no default, the statement simply does 
nothing and moves on, which can lead to "silent" bugs that are hard to track down. 
 
 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ4  من9     Page 4 of 9   السؤال الثالث  8 درجات  8 Marks Question 3  
انظر إلﻰ مقتطف كود بﺎيثون التﺎلي :  Consider the following Python code 
snippet: 
def process_data(data): 
    if isinstance(data, int): 
        return data * 2 
    elif isinstance(data, str): 
        return data.upper() 
    elif isinstance(data, list): 
        return [item for item in data if item > 0] 
    else: 
        return "Unsupported data type" 
 
value1 = 10 
value2 = "hello world" 
value3 = [-1, 2, 0, 5] 
value4 = 3.14 
 
print(process_data(value1)) 
print(process_data(value2)) 
print(process_data(value3)) 
print(process_data(value4)) 
أ( مﺎ هو نﺎتج هذا  ؟جمﺎنربلا  
  
ب( اشرح كيف يوضﺢ هذا المثﺎل اﻻنواع الدينﺎميكيﺔ 
والتﺣقﻖ الدينﺎميكي من أنواع البيﺎنﺎت. نﺎقش تﺄثير هذه  
الخﺻﺎئص علﻰ مرونﺔ  جمﺎنربلا واﻷخطﺎء المﺣتملﺔ أثنﺎء 
التشغيل،  ًﺔنرﺎقم بلغﺔ ذات كتﺎبﺔ ثﺎبتﺔ مثل C ++أو 
Java.  a) What is the output of this program?   
b) Explain how this example demonstrates 
dynamic typing  and dynamic type 
checking . Discuss the implications of these 
characteristics on program ﬂexibility and 
potential runtime errors, compared to a 
statically typed language like C++ or Java. 
a) Program Output  
The program will produce the following output: 
 
20 
HELLO WORLD 
[2, 5] 
Unsupported data type 
 
b) Dynamic Typing and Type Checking 
This snippet is a perfect illustration of how Python handles data types compared to stricter 
languages. 
1. Demonstration of Dynamic Typing 
Dynamic Typing  refers to the fact that variables in Python are not "bound" to a speciﬁc type. 
 In the code, the function process_data(data) does not specify what data must be. 
 The same parameter name (data) successfully holds an int, then a str, then a list 
during diƯerent calls.  
2. Demonstration of Dynamic Type Checking 
Dynamic Type Checking  means that the type safety of an operation is veriﬁed at runtime  
(while the program is running). 
 The isinstance() checks happen as the code executes. 
 Python "interrogates" the object at the moment the function is called to decide which 
logic path to take. 
 If you passed a type that didn't support a speciﬁc operation (and didn't have the else 
safety net), the program would only crash when it reached that speciﬁc line of code. 
 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ5  من9     Page 5 of 9  السؤال الرابع  8 درجات  8  Marks Question 4  
معﺎلجﺔ اﻻستثنﺎءات هي آليﺔ منظمﺔ للتعﺎمل مع أخطﺎء 
وقت التشغيل أو الﺣﺎﻻت غير اﻻعتيﺎديﺔ ﻓي البرنﺎمج .  
  
أ( ﺻف المزايﺎ الرئيسيﺔ ﻻستخدام آليﺔ  قويﺔ لمعﺎلجﺔ  
اﻻستثنﺎءات )مثل كتل try-catch ﻓي Java أو C  ++
أو C (# ًﺔنرﺎقم بتقنيﺎت التﺣقﻖ من اﻷخطﺎء التقليديﺔ  
)مثل إرجﺎع رموز الخطﺄ، أو استخدام عﻼمﺎت الخطﺄ  
العﺎمﺔ(.  
  
ب( نﺎقش قضيتين تﺻميميتين هﺎمتين يجب علﻰ 
مﺻممي اللغﺎت مراعﺎتهمﺎ عند تطبيﻖ آليﺔ معﺎلجﺔ 
اﻻستثنﺎءات.  Exception handling is a structured 
mechanism for dealing with runtime errors or 
unusual conditions in a program. 
a) Describe the primary beneﬁts of using a 
robust exception handling mechanism (like 
try-catch blocks in Java, C++, or C#) 
compared to traditional error-checking 
techniques (e.g., returning error codes, using 
global error ﬂags).  
b) Discuss two signiﬁcant design issues  that 
language designers must consider when 
implementing an exception handling 
mechanism.  
a) Beneﬁts of Exception Handling  
Before modern exception handling, programmers relied on "error codes" (e.g., a function 
returning -1 on failure) or global ﬂags (like errno in C). Moving to try-catch blocks provide 
several key advantages: 
 Separation of Error-Handling Code from "Normal" Code: In traditional error-checking, 
every function call is followed by an if statement to check for success. This "clutters" 
the logic. Exception handling allows you to wrap the main logic in one block and 
handle all potential errors in a separate section, making the code much more 
readable. 
 Automatic Error Propagation: Traditional error codes must be manually passed back 
up through every single function in the call stack. Exceptions, however, propagate 
automatically. If a low-level function throws an error, the program searches up the 
stack until it ﬁnds a handler, saving developers from writing repetitive "pass-back" 
logic. 
 Grouping and Categorizing Errors: Exceptions are typically objects organized in a 
hierarchy (e.g., IOException is a parent to FileNotFoundException). This allows a 
programmer to catch a speciﬁc error or a broad category of errors using a single catch 
block, which is impossible with simple integer error codes. 
 Guaranteed Cleanup: Mechanisms like the ﬁnally block ensure that critical resources 
(like database connections or open ﬁles) are closed regardless of whether an error 
occurred, preventing memory leaks and orphaned resources. 
 
b) Design Issues for Language Designers 
Implementing exception handling requires making fundamental decisions about how the 
language behaves when things go wrong. Two signiﬁcant design issues include: 
1. Exception Binding: Checked vs. Unchecked Exceptions 
Designers must decide if the compiler should force the programmer to handle certain 
exceptions. 
 Checked Exceptions (e.g., Java): The compiler ensures that a function either catches 
a speciﬁc exception or declares that it might throw it. This increases safety but can 
lead to "noisy" code where programmers write empty catch blocks just to satisfy the 
compiler. 
 Unchecked Exceptions (e.g., C#, Python, C++): The language allows any exception to 
be thrown without explicit declaration. This makes the code cleaner and more ﬂexible 
but increases the risk of a program crashing at runtime because a developer forgot an 
error could occur. 
 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ6  من9     Page 6 of 9  2. Continuation vs. Resumption Model  
This issue determines where the program goes after an exception is handled. 
 Termination/Continuation Model (Most common): When an exception is caught, the 
block of code that caused the error is abandoned. Execution continues from the 
catch/ﬁnally block. This is simpler to implement and generally safer. 
 Resumption Model (Rare, e.g., PL/I): The handler has the option to "ﬁx" the problem 
and then tell the program to return to the exact line of code that caused the error to try 
again. While powerful, this is extremely di Ưicult to implement safely because t he 
system state may have changed during the error. 
 
 السؤال الخامس  8 درجات  8 Marks Question 5  
لنﻔترض دالﺔ  الكود الزائف  ﺔيلﺎتلا modify(X, Y) 
والدالﺔ الرئيسيﺔ التﺎليﺔ :  Consider the following pseudo -code function 
modify(X, Y) and the following main: 
 
function modify(X, Y): 
    X = X * 2 
    Y = Y + X 
    print("Inside modify: X =", X, ", Y =", Y) 
… 
// main 
A = 5 
B = 10 
modify(A, B) 
print("After modify: A =", A, ", B =", B)  
أ( ﺣدد القيمتين النهﺎئيتين لـ A  و B إذا تم تمرير X و Y 
بﺎستخدام طريقﺔ تمرير النتيجﺔ. اشرح طريقﺔ استنتﺎجك  
خطوة بخطوة.   
  
ب( ﺣدد القيمتين النهﺎئيتين لـ A و B إذا تم تمرير X و 
Y بﺎستخدام طريقﺔ تمرير القيمﺔ والنتيجﺔ. اشرح طريقﺔ 
استنتﺎجك خطوة  بخطوة.   a) Determine the ﬁnal values of A and B if X 
and Y are passed using pass-by-result . 
Explain your reasoning step-by-step.  
b) Determine the ﬁnal values of A and B if X 
and Y are passed using pass-by-value-
result. Explain your reasoning step-by-step.  
a) Pass-by-Result 
In pass-by-result, no data is passed to the function when it is called. Instead, the formal 
parameters (X and Y) act as local variables initialized to a default value (usually undeﬁned or 
0). When the function exits, the ﬁnal values of these local variables are assigned back to the 
actual arguments (A and B). 
Step-by-Step Reasoning: 
1. Call to modify(A, B): A and B are passed, but their values (5 and 10) are ignored. 
2. Initialization: X and Y start with uninitialized or default values (let's assume 0 for this 
calculation). 
3. Operation 1 (X = X * 2): X = 0 * 2 = 0. 
4. Operation 2 (Y = Y + X): Y = 0 + 0 = 0. 
5. Inside Print: Outputs X = 0, Y = 0. 
6. Function Exit: The ﬁnal values of X and Y are copied into A and B. 
o 𝐴 =  𝑋→𝐴 =  0 
o 𝐵 =  𝑌→𝐵 =  0 
Final Values: A = 0, B = 0  
(Note: If the language leaves them uninitialized, the result could be an error or garbage values, 
but logically the result is the assignment of the ﬁnal local state.)  
 
 
 
 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ7  من9     Page 7 of 9  b) Pass-by-Value-Result 
Pass-by-value-result (also known as "copy-in, copy-out") is a combination of pass-by-value 
and pass-by-result. 
1. Copy-In: The values of the actual arguments (A, B) are copied into the formal 
parameters (X, Y) at the start. 
2. Execution: The function operates on the local copies. 
3. Copy-Out: When the function ﬁnishes, the ﬁnal local values are copied back into the 
original variables. 
Step-by-Step Reasoning: 
1. Initialization (Copy-In): 
o X = A (so X = 5) 
o Y = B (so Y = 10) 
2. Operation 1 (X = X * 2): 
o X = 5 * 2 = 10 
3. Operation 2 (Y = Y + X): 
o Y = 10 + 10 = 20 
4. Inside Print: Outputs X = 10, Y = 20. 
5. Function Exit (Copy-Out): 
o The ﬁnal value of X (10) is copied back to A. 
o The ﬁnal value of Y (20) is copied back to B. 
Final Values: A = 10, B = 20  
 السؤالالسادس   8 درجات  8 Points Question  6  
 ّدعُي التزامن ﺎًبنﺎج بﺎلﻎ اﻷهميﺔ ﻓي البرمجﺔ الﺣديثﺔ، ولكنه  
ريثُي  ٍتﺎيدﺣت مثل ﺣﺎﻻت التنﺎﻓس.  
  
أ( فّرع  نمازت المنافسة ﻓي سيﺎق البرمجﺔ المتزامنﺔ  .
اشرح كيف مدختسُي تزامن المنﺎﻓسﺔ  ّلﺣل ﺣﺎﻻت التنﺎﻓس.  
  
ب( اشرح كيف نكمُي استخدام إشﺎرة ثنﺎئيﺔ لمنع ﺣﺎلﺔ  
التنﺎﻓس التي وﺻﻔتهﺎ ﻓي الجزء  )أ(. ﺻف عمليﺎت  
اﻹشﺎرة )اﻻنتظﺎر/P واﻹشﺎرة/V.(  Concurrency is a critical aspect of modern 
programming, but it introduces challenges 
like race conditions. 
a) Deﬁne what competition synchronization  
is in the context of concurrent programming. 
Explain how competition synchronization  is 
needed to solve race conditions.  
b) Explain how a binary semaphore  can be 
used to prevent the race condition you 
described in part (a). Describe the operations 
of a semaphore (wait/P and signal/V).  
a) Competition Synchronization and Race Conditions  
Competition Synchronization  is a mechanism used to coordinate access to a shared 
resource when multiple processes or threads compete for it. Its primary goal is to ensure 
mutual exclusion , meaning only one process can access the resource at any given time. 
How it solves Race Conditions 
A Race Condition  occurs when two or more threads access shared data and try to change it 
at the same time. Because the thread scheduling algorithm can swap between threads at any 
moment, you can't predict the order in which the threads will attempt to access the data. 
By using competition synchronization, we deﬁne a Critical Section —a piece of code that 
accesses the shared resource. Synchronization ensures that if one thread is executing in its 
critical section, all other threads are "locked out" until the ﬁrst thread ﬁnishes. This prevents 
the interleaved execution that causes data corruption. 
 
b) Binary Semaphores 
A Binary Semaphore  is a synchronization tool that acts like a digital "lock." It is an integer 
variable that, in a binary context, only takes the values 0 or 1. 
 1 (Open):  The resource is available. 
 0 (Locked):  The resource is currently in use. 
 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ8  من9     Page 8 of 9  Semaphore Operations  
To manage this lock, semaphores use two atomic operations: 
1. Wait: 
o When a thread wants to enter a critical section, it calls Wait. 
o If the semaphore is 1, it is decremented to 0, and the thread proceeds. 
o If the semaphore is 0, the thread is blocked (put to sleep) until the value 
becomes 1 again. 
2. Signal: 
o When a thread ﬁnishes its critical section, it calls Signal. 
o The semaphore value is incremented back to 1. 
o If there are other threads waiting, one of them is woken up to take its turn. 
 
Preventing Race Condition 
To prevent racing conditions, you simply wrap the "dangerous" code with these two calls: 
 
Wait(S);       // Check if the door is open and lock it 
/* CRITICAL SECTION (e.g., balance = balance + deposit) */ 
Signal(S);     // Unlock the door for the next person 
 
Where S is the semaphore used. Because these operations are atomic (they cannot be 
interrupted halfway through), it is impossible for two threads to pass the Wait check at the 
exact same time. 
 
 السؤالالسابع )اﻷخير(   8 درجات  8 Marks Question  7 (ﬁnal) 
لنﻔترض مﻔهوم دالﺔ map، التي ﻖّبطُت دالﺔ ةﺎطعُم علﻰ  
كل عنﺻر من عنﺎﺻر القﺎئمﺔ ديعُتو قﺎئمﺔ جديدة 
بﺎلنتﺎئج.   
  
أ( بﺎستخدام أسلوب البرمجﺔ الوظيﻔيﺔ )مثل استخدام  
الشﻔرة الزائﻔﺔ  ةﺎﺣوتسُملا من لغﺎت Lisp/Scheme أو  
Haskell(، اكتب ﺎًﻔيرعت  ﺔلادل  map تﺄخذ دالﺔ f وقﺎئمﺔ 
lst كمعﺎمﻼت. يجب أن تستخدم  دالﺔ map اﻻستدعﺎء  
الذاتي  ﺔجلﺎعمل القﺎئمﺔ .  
  
ب( نّيب كيف  نكمُي استخدام  ﺔلاد  map الخﺎﺻﺔ بك  
للقيﺎم بمﺎ يلي:  
1 .ﺔﻔعﺎضُم كل عدد ﻓي القﺎئمﺔ  )1 2 3 4  5 .(  
2 .تربيع كل عدد ﻓي القﺎئمﺔ )1 2 3 4 5 .(  Consider the concept of a map function, 
which applies a given function to each 
element of a list and returns a new list of the 
results. 
a) In a functional style (e.g., using pseudo-
code inspired by Lisp/Scheme or Haskell), 
write a deﬁnition for a map function that 
takes a function f and a list lst as arguments. 
Your map function should use recursion to 
process the list.  
b) Demonstrate how your map function would 
be used to: 
 i. Double each number in the list (1 2 3 4 5).  
ii. Square each number in the list (1 2 3 4 5).  
a) Functional Deﬁnition of map  
In functional programming, the map function is typically deﬁned using recursion  and pattern 
matching  (or head/tail decomposition). 
Using a pseudo-code inspired by Scheme/Lisp, we can deﬁne it as follows: 
 
(deﬁne (map f lst) 
  (if (null? lst)                            ; Base case: Is the list empty? 
      '()                                             ; Return an empty list 
      (cons (f (car lst))               ; Apply f to the ﬁrst element (car) 
            (map f (cdr lst))           ; Recurse on the rest of the list (cdr) 
      ) 
  ) 
)     
 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ9  من9     Page 9 of 9   
b) Demonstrating map in Action 
To use the map function, we pass it a speciﬁc operation (often deﬁned as a lambda or 
anonymous function) and the list (1 2 3 4 5). 
i. Double each number in the list 
To double the numbers, we pass a function that takes x and returns x * 2. 
Pseudo-code:  
 
(map (lambda (x) (* x 2)) '(1 2 3 4 5)) 
 
ii. Square each number in the list 
To square the numbers, we pass a function that takes x and returns x * x (or x^2). 
Pseudo-code:  
 
(map (lambda (x) (* x x)) '(1 2 3 4 5))

السؤال الثاني  4 درجات  Grades 4  Question 2  
ما الذي يؤثر على موثوقية لغة  البرمجة؟  What aƯects a programming language's 
reliability? 
 
اﻹجابة:   
لاقُي إن البرنامج موثوق إذا كان  يعمل اًقفو لمواصفاته في 
جميع الظروف. فيما يلي خصاﺋص  ةغللا التي تؤثر على  
موثوقية البرنامج:   
1. فحص النوع: فحص  النوع هو عملية اكتشاف 
أخطاء النوع في البرنامج،  ًءاوس أثناء التجميع  
أو أثناء التنفيذ. ززعُي هذا الفحص موثوقية 
اللغة، لضفُيو  فحص وقت التجميع اًرظن 
ﻻرتفاع  تكلفة فحص وقت التشغيل. للقُي الكشف 
المبكر عن اﻷخطاء من تكاليف اﻹصﻼح. 
2.  معالجة اﻻستثناءات: نّكمُت معالجة اﻻستثناءات  
البرنامج من اكتشاف أخطاء وقت التشغيل أو 
الظروف غير العادية وإدارتها، مما نّسحُي 
الموثوقية من خﻼل تمكين اﻻسترداد واستمرار  
التنفيذ. 
3. اﻷسماء المستعارة: يحدث اﻻسم  المستعار عندما 
ريشُت أسماء متعددة في البرنامج إلى نفس خلية  
الذاكرة، وهي ميزة ربتعُت على نطاق واسع 
محفوفة بالمخاطر. في حين أن معظم اللغات 
تسمﺢ باﻻسم المستعار ) ،ًﻼثم عبر المؤشرات  
أو المراجع(، إﻻ  هنأ قد يؤدي  إلى آثار جانبية 
غير مقصودة - تعديل البيانات  من خﻼل اسم  
واحد يؤثر على جميع اﻷسماء المستعارة. دّيقُت  
بعض اللغات استخدام اﻻسم المستعار لتحسين 
الموثوقية، بينما تسمﺢ به لغات أخرى للتغلب 
على قيود تجريد البيانات.  
4. سهولة القراءة والكتابة: تؤثر سهولة القراءة 
والكتابة بشكل مباشر على موثوقية البرنامج. إذا  
لم تسمﺢ لغة البرمجة بالتعبير الواضﺢ  
والطبيعي عن الخوارزميات،  دقف يلجأ 
المطورون إلى حلول معقدة أكثر عرضة  
لﻸخطاء. فالكود اﻷسهل في  الكتابة يكون أكثر 
صحة  . ًةفاضإ إلى ذلك، تؤثر سهولة القراءة 
على  ٍّلك من  التطوير والصيانة،  فالبرامج صعبة  
القراءة يصعب كتابتها وتعديلها بشكل صحيﺢ  
دون أخطاء .  Answer: 
A program is said to be reliable if it performs   
to its speciﬁcations under all conditions. The 
following are language features that aƯect 
program reliability: 
1) Type checking: Type checking is the 
process of detecting type errors in a 
program, either at compile time or 
during execution. It enhances 
language reliability, with compile-
time checking being preferable due to 
the high cost of runtime checking. 
Early error detection reduces repair 
costs.   
2) Exception Handling: Exception 
handling allows a program to detect 
and manage runtime errors or 
unusual conditions, improving 
reliability by enabling recovery and 
continued execution. 
3) Aliasing: Aliasing occurs when 
multiple names in a program refer to 
the same memory cell, which is 
widely considered a risky feature. 
While most languages allow aliasing 
(e.g., via pointers or references), it 
can lead to unintended side e Ưects—
modifying data through one name 
aƯecting all aliases. Some languages 
restrict aliasing to improve reliability, 
while others permit it to work around 
limitations in data abstraction.  
4) Readability and Writability: 
Readability and writability directly 
impact a program's reliability. If a 
language doesn't allow clear, natural 
expression of algorithms, developers 
may resort to convoluted solutions 
that are more error-prone. Easier-to-
write code is more likely to be 
correct. Additionally, readability 
aƯects both development and 
maintenance—hard-to-read 
programs are more di Ưicult to write 
correctly and modify without 
introducing errors.  
 
 السؤال الثالث  4 درجات  Grades 4  Question 3  
خذ بعين اﻻعتبار برنامج JavaScript الهيكلي التالي :  Consider the following JavaScript skeletal 
program : 
 
// The main program 
var x;     //Declaration 1 
function sub1 () { 
        var x;  //Declaration 2 
        function sub2 () { 
         …. 
       } 
} 
function sub3 )( { 
….. 
} 
 
افترض  نأ تنفيذ هذا البرنامج يتم بالترتيب التالي:  
main يستدعي sub1  
sub1 يستدعي sub2  
sub2 يستدعي sub3  
بافتراض تحديد النطاق الثابت، أي تعريف للمتغير x هو  
التعريف الصحيﺢ لﻺشارة  إلى x فيما يلي ؟  
1 .sub1 
2 .sub2 
3 .sub3  Assume that the execution of this program is 
in the following unit order  : 
main calls sub1 
sub1 calls sub2 
sub2 calls sub3 
Assuming static scoping, in the following, 
which declaration of x is the correct one for a 
reference to x  ? 
i. sub1 
ii. sub2 
iii. sub3 
اﻹجابة:  
  
بما أن  لاؤسلا يتناول النطاق الثابت فقط، فﻼ أهمية ﻷي  
برنامج فرعي يستدعي اﻵخر. لحُي النطاق الثابت أثناء 
التجميع ويعتمد على حدود البرامج الفرعية ومكان  نﻼعإ  
تعريفها.   
  
Sub1 :ﻷن sub1 فّرعُي x في البداية  
) Declaration 2(، مدختسُي هذا التعريف في جميع  
أنحاء نطاق sub1 .  
  
Sub2 :ﻷن sub2 فّرعُم ضمن نطاق sub1 .لذلك،  
فإن المرجع مدختسُملا  ـل x هو نفسه مدختسُملا  يف sub1،  
أي Declaration 2 .  
  
Sub3 :ﻷن sub3 فّرعُم ضمن البرنامج الرﺋيسي،  
وليس في sub1، مدختسُيو النطاق الثابت، لذا فإن x  
مدختسُملا في هذا البرنامج الفرعي هو x في  
Declaration 1 .ﻻ رثؤُي استدعاؤه في sub2، ﻷن  
استدعاء البرنامج الفرعي في  النطاق الديناميكي فقط يؤثر  
على نطاق المتغيرات في البرنامج الفرعي .  Answer  : 
 
Because the question considers only static 
scoping, it becomes irrelevant to what 
subprogram called the other. Static scoping 
is solved at compile time and depends on the 
boundaries of the subprograms and where 
their deﬁnition is declared   . 
Sub1: Because sub1 deﬁnes x at the very 
beginning (declaration 2) this declaration is 
used throughout the scope of the sub1   . 
Sub2: Because sub2 is deﬁned within the 
scope of sub1. Therefore, the reference used 
for x is the same as sub1, that is, declaration 
2 . 
Sub3: Because sub3 is deﬁned within the 
main, not in sub1 and static scoping is used 
so the x used in this subprogram is the x in 
declaration 1. The fact that it is called in sub2 
has no eƯect, because only in dynamic 
scoping does subprogram calling a Ưect the 
scope of variables in a subprogram.  
 
السؤال الرابع  4 درجات  Grades 4  Question 4  
قم بتعريف الترتيب الرﺋيسي للصف والترتيب الرﺋيسي 
للعمود في المصفوفات، مع إعطاء مثال للغات التي تدعم  
كل ترتيب.   Deﬁne row major order and column major 
order in arrays, give an example of languages 
that support each order. 
اﻹجابة:   
يكمن الفرق بين ترتيب الصفوف الرﺋيسية وترتيب  
اﻷعمدة الرﺋيسية في كيفية تخزين المصفوفات متعددة 
اﻷبعاد في الذاكرة الخطية )RAM.(  
  
ترتيب الصفوف الرئيسية  
التعريف: نﱠزخُت العناصر اًفص بصف )من اليسار إلى  
اليمين، ومن أعلى  إلى  أسفل .(  
مَدختسُي في: C، وC++، وPython )الوضع 
اﻻفتراضي في  NumPy(، وJava، ومعظم لغات  
البرمجة  ةيلاع المستوى .  
  
ترتيب اﻷعمدة الرئيسية  
التعريف: نﱠزخُت العناصر  اًدومع بعمود )من أعلى إلى  
أسفل، ومن اليسار إلى اليمين(.  
مَدختسُي في: Fortran .  Answer: 
The diƯerence between row -major order and 
column-major order lies in how multi-
dimensional arrays are stored in linear 
memory (RAM). 
 
 
Row-Major Order 
Deﬁnition: Elements are stored row by row 
(left to right, top to bottom) . 
Used in: C, C++, Python (NumPy default), 
Java, and most high-level languages. 
 
Column-Major Order 
Deﬁnition: Elements are stored column by 
column (top to bottom, left to right)  . 
Used in: Fortran. 
 
السؤال الخامس )اﻷخير(   4 درجات  Grades 4  Question 5  (Final) 
خذ بعين اﻻعتبار برنامج C التالي:  Consider the following C program:  
int fun(int *i) { 
       *i += 5; 
       return 4; 
} 
void main() { 
       int x = 3; 
       x = x + fun(&x); 
} 
ما قيمة x بعد عبارة التعيين في main، بافتراض أن  :  
أ. يتم تقييم المتغيرات من اليسار إلى اليمين.  
ب. يتم تقييم المتغيرات  من اليمين  ىلإ اليسار .  What is the value of x after the assignment 
statement in main, assuming 
a. operands are evaluated left to right  . 
b. operands are evaluated right to left.  
اﻹجابة:  
  
التقييم من اليسار إلى اليمين:  دنع تقييم تﻼماعُملا من 
اليسار إلى  اليمين في  ةيلمع التعيين، يبدأ التعبير بتقييم  
لماعُملا اﻷول على  اليسار؛ ويتم ذلك بالحصول  على  قيمة  
x في الذاكرة )قيمة x هي 3 .(لماعُملا الثاني لعامل +  
هو استدعاء لدالة ررمُت  ناونع x في الذاكرة )fun(&x)  (
لماعُمك. تستقبل الدالة  العنوان لماعُمك كمؤشر )*i (إلى 
عدد  صحيﺢ؛ وبالتالي، فإن *i هو مؤشر إلى عنوان x،  
ويزداد موقع الذاكرة الذي ريشُي إليه *i بمقدار 5، مما 
يجعل قيمة x 8 .عجرُت الدالة  القيمة 4، والتي مدختسُت في  
التعبير كقيمة لماعُملا الثاني. وبالتالي،  نإف قيمة تعبير  
التعيين هي 3  +4، والنتيجة هي x = 7 .  Answer : 
Left-to-right Evaluation: When operands are 
evaluated left to right in the assignment, the 
expression starts by evaluating the ﬁrst 
operand on the left; this is done by obtaining 
the value of x in memory (the value of x is 3). 
The second operand of the + operator is a call 
to a function passing as a parameter the 
address of x in memory (fun(&x)). The 
function receives as a parameter the address 
as a pointer (*i) to integer; therefore, *i is a 
pointer to the address of x, the memory 
location pointed to by *i is incremented by 5, 
making the value of x 8. The function returns 
  
التقييم من اليمين إلى اليسار  :في  عملية التقييم من اليمين 
إلى اليسار لعبارة التعيين في البرنامج الرﺋيسي، يتم 
الحصول  على  قيمة لماعُملا من لماعُملا اﻷيمن  ًﻻوأ. 
لذلك، ىعدتسُت الدالة  fun ،ًﻻوأ  وكما هو موضﺢ ،اًقباس  
رّيغُت الدالة قيمة x بزيادتها بمقدار 5؛ قيمة x بعد 
استدعاﺋها هي 8 .مع ذلك،  عجرُت الدالة  القيمة 4، ويكون 
التعبير بعد حساب لماعُملا اﻷول من اليمين هو x=x+4  .
بالحصول على قيمة x في  الذاكرة لماعُملل الثاني، تكون 
نتيجة التعيين x=8+4=12 .  4, which is used in the expression as the 
value of the second operand. Therefore, the 
value of the assignment expression is 3+4, 
and the result is x=7    
Right to left Evaluation: In a right to left 
evaluation of the assignment expression in 
the main program, the operand's value is 
obtained from the right most operand ﬁrst. 
Therefore, the function fun is called ﬁrst, and 
as explained above, the function alters the 
value of x by incrementing it by 5; the value of 
x after the call to the function is 8. However, 
the function returns the value of 4, and the 
expression after the evaluation of the ﬁrst 
operand from the right is x=x+4. By obtaining 
the value of x in memory for the second 
operand, the result of the assignment is 
x=8+4=12.

 لوﻷا لاؤسلا   4 درجات  4 Points Question  1 
 ما هي إيجابيات وسلبيات استخدام كلمات محجوزةﻓي 
تحديد جمل مركبة؟  What are the pros and cons of using unique 
closing reserved words on compound 
statements? 
 
Answer: 
 Pros: 
o Readability:  Unique closing reserved words (e.g., end if, end while in Ada) 
make it easier to identify the end of a compound statement, improving code 
clarity. 
o Error Detection:  They help compilers detect mismatched or missing 
delimiters, reducing syntax errors. 
o Nesting Support:  They simplify understanding deeply nested control 
structures by explicitly marking the end of each block. 
 Cons: 
o Verbosity:  Requiring unique closing words (instead of just braces {}) can make 
code longer and more tedious to write. 
o Learning Curve: Programmers must memorize additional reserved words, 
which may be language-speciﬁc (e.g., ﬁ for if in shell scripting). 
 
السؤال الثاني  4 درجات  4 Points Question 2  
قم بوصف مﺷكلة تمرير المصفوﻓات متعددة اﻷبعاد  
كمعلمات.  Describe the problem of passing 
multidimension arrays as parameters. 
 
Answer: 
The key issue is storage mapping —how multidimensional arrays are stored in memory. 
Challenges include: 
 Size Speciﬁcation:  The compiler needs to know all but the ﬁrst dimension to 
compute memory o Ưsets correctly.  In C, if a function accepts int arr[][], it won’t 
compile; you must specify int arr[][N]. 
 Flexibility Loss:  Fixed dimensions limit the function’s reusability for arrays of di Ưerent 
sizes. 
 Pointer Decay:  In some languages (like C), arrays decay into pointers, losing 
dimension information and complicating bounds checking. 
 
 السؤال الثالث  4 درجات  4 Points Question 3  
ﻓكر ﻓي البرنامج التالي المكتوب بلغة C:  Consider the following program written in C 
syntax: 
void swap(int a, int b) { 
int temp; 
temp = a; 
a = b; 
b = temp; 
} 
void main() { 
int value = 2, list[5] = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5}; 
swap(value, list[0]); 
swap(list[0], list[1]); 
swap(value, list[value]); 
} 
 
 ٍّلكل من طرق تمرير المعامﻼت  التالية، ما هي قيم  
متغيري value وlist بعد  ٍّلك من استدعاءات الدالة  
swap الثﻼثة؟  
  
أ. تم تمريرها بواسطة value  
ب. تم تمريرها بواسطة reference  
ج. تم تمريرها بواسطة value-result  For each of the following parameter -passing 
methods, what are all values of the variables 
value and list after each of the three calls to 
swap ? 
a. Passed by value 
b. Passed by reference 
c. Passed by value-result 
 
Answer: 
The original state before any swaps is: 
 value = 2 
 list = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5} 
 
a. Passed by Value (Call by Value)  
In pass-by-value , a copy of the argument is passed to the function. Changes inside swap do 
not aƯect the original variables.  
After swap(value, list[0]) 
 Copies: a = 2 (from value), b = 1 (from list[0]) 
 Inside swap: a and b are swapped (a=1, b=2), but originals remain unchanged. 
 No change to value or list. 
o value = 2, list = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5} 
After swap(list[0], list[1]) 
 Copies: a = 1 (list[0]), b = 2 (list[1]) 
 Inside swap: a and b are swapped (a=2, b=1), but originals remain unchanged. 
 No change to list. 
o value = 2, list = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5} 
After swap(value, list[value]) 
 list[value] = list[2] = 3 
 Copies: a = 2 (value), b = 3 (list[2]) 
 Inside swap: a and b are swapped (a=3, b=2), but originals remain unchanged. 
 No change to value or list. 
Final state: 
 value = 2 
 list = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5} 
 
b. Passed by Reference (Call by Reference)  
In pass-by-reference , the function receives aliases (references) to the original variables. 
Changes inside swap aƯect the originals.  
After swap(value, list[0]) 
 a refers to value, b refers to list[0] 
 Swapping modiﬁes value and list[0]: 
o value = 1 
o list = {2, 2, 3, 4, 5} 
After swap(list[0], list[1]) 
 a refers to list[0] (2), b refers to list[1] (2) 
 Swapping does nothing (both are 2). 
o value = 1 
o list = {2, 2, 3, 4, 5} 
After swap(value, list[value]) 
 value = 1, so list[value] = list[1] = 2 
 a refers to value (1), b refers to list[1] (2) 
 Swapping modiﬁes value and list[1]: 
o value = 2 
o list = {2, 1, 3, 4, 5} 
Final state:  
 value = 2 
 list = {2, 1, 3, 4, 5} 
 
 
c. Passed by Value -Result (Copy -In/Copy-Out) 
In pass-by-value-result , the function works with copies of the arguments, but the ﬁnal 
values are copied back to the originals after the function ends. 
After swap(value, list[0]) 
1. Copy-in:  a = 2 (value), b = 1 (list[0]) 
2. Inside swap: a and b are swapped (a=1, b=2) 
3. Copy-out:  value = 1, list[0] = 2 
o value = 1 
o list = {2, 2, 3, 4, 5} 
After swap(list[0], list[1]) 
1. Copy-in:  a = 2 (list[0]), b = 2 (list[1]) 
2. Inside swap: a and b are swapped (a=2, b=2) (no change) 
3. Copy-out:  list[0] = 2, list[1] = 2 
o value = 1 
o list = {2, 2, 3, 4, 5} 
After swap(value, list[value]) 
 value = 1, so list[value] = list[1] = 2 
1. Copy-in:  a = 1 (value), b = 2 (list[1]) 
2. Inside swap: a and b are swapped (a=2, b=1) 
3. Copy-out:  value = 2, list[1] = 1 
o Final state: 
 value = 2 
 list = {2, 1, 3, 4, 5} 
Final state (same as pass-by-reference in this case):  
 value = 2 
 list = {2, 1, 3, 4, 5} 
 
السؤال الرابع  4 درجات  4 Points Question 4  
ما الفرق بين سجل التنﺷيط ومثيل سجل التنﺷيط؟  ِطعأي  
 ًﻻاثم لتوضيح إجابتك.   What is the di Ưerence between an activation 
record and an activation record instance? 
Give an example to explain your answer. 
 
 
Answer: 
 Activation Record (AR):  A template  or layout for the data structure used to manage a 
single subroutine call (e.g., return address, parameters, local variables). This is 
created at compile time. 
 Activation Record Instance (ARI):  A concrete instance  of that template created at 
runtime for each speciﬁc subroutine call. 
Example:  
 For a function foo(int x, int y), the activation record  deﬁnes that it must store x, y, a 
return address, and local variables. 
 When foo(5, 10) is called, an ARI is created on the stack with x=5, y=10, and the 
current return address. 
 
 
 (السؤال الخامس )اﻷخير  4 درجات  4 Points Question 5 (Final)  
خذ بعين اﻻعتبار برنامج C++  التالي :  Consider the following C++ program:  
#include <iostream> 
#include <string> 
// Base class 1: Animal 
class Animal { 
public: 
    std::string type = "Generic Animal";  
    virtual void move() { std::cout << type << " moves generically." << std::endl; } 
    virtual void eat() {std:: cout << type << " eats food." << std::endl; } 
    virtual ~Animal() {} // Virtual destructor for polymorphism 
}; 
// Base class 2: Bird 
class Bird { 
public: 
    std::string type = "Generic Bird";  
    virtual void fly() {std::cout << type << " flies!" << std::endl; } 
    virtual void eat() {std::cout << type << " eats seeds." << std::endl; } 
    virtual ~Bird() {} // Virtual destructor for polymorphism 
}; 
// Derived class: Penguin (inherits from both Animal and Bird) 
class Penguin : public Animal, public Bird { 
public: 
    Penguin() {        Animal::type = "Penguin (Animal)";  
                              Bird::type = "Penguin (Bird)";                 } 
    void move() override { std::cout << "Penguin waddles." << std::endl; } 
    void fly() override {std::cout << "Penguin cannot fly!" << std::endl; }  
    void eat() override {std::cout << "Penguin eats fish!" << std::endl; }  
}; 
int main() { 
    Penguin penguin;  
    Animal* animalPtr = &penguin;  
    std::cout << "Animal type: " << animalPtr- >type << std::endl;  
    animalPtr- >move();  
    animalPtr- >eat(); 
    Bird* birdPtr = &penguin;  
    std::cout << "Bird type: " << birdPtr- >type << std::endl;  
    birdPtr- >fly();  
    birdPtr->eat (); 
    return 0; 
} 
أجب عن  اﻷسئلة التالية :  
أ( ما هو ناتج البرنامج المذكور أعﻼه؟  
ب( ارسم مثيﻼت CIR وجدول vtable للفئات المذكورة 
أعﻼه .  
ج( ماذا لو لم يتجاوز)Override( Class Penguin 
أمر eat()؟ ما التغييرات المطلوبة للبرنامج  ؟يسيئرلا  Answer the following:  
a) What is the output of the above 
program? 
b) Draw the CIR instances and vtable of 
the above classes. 
c) What if Class Penguin did not 
Override eat()? What changes are 
needed to the main program? 
Answer: 
a) The program produces the following output: 
Animal type: Penguin (Animal)   
Penguin waddles.   
Penguin eats fish!   
Bird type: Penguin (Bird)   
Penguin cannot fly!   
Penguin eats fish!   
 
b)  CIR Instances and VTable Layout 
Class Instance Representation (CIR) for Penguin 
 
A Penguin object contains: 
Animal subobject: 
vptr (pointer to Animal's vtable) 
type ("Penguin (Animal)") 
Bird subobject: 
vptr (pointer to Bird's vtable) 
type ("Penguin (Bird)") 
 
VTables for Each Class 
Class VTable Entries  
Animal move() → Animal::move()  (but overridden by  Penguin) 
eat() → Animal::eat() (overridden by Penguin) 
~Animal() (destructor) 
Bird ﬂy() → Bird::ﬂy()  (overridden by  Penguin) 
eat() → Bird::eat() (overridden by Penguin) 
~Bird() (destructor) 
Penguin Animal vtable part:  
move() → Penguin::move() 
eat() → Penguin::eat() 
Bird vtable part: 
ﬂy() → Penguin::ﬂy() 
eat() → Penguin::eat() 
If Penguin Did Not Override eat() 
Problem:  
Both Animal and Bird have eat(), leading to ambiguity . The compiler will fail with an error: 
error: request for member 'eat' is ambiguous 
Solution:  
Modiﬁed main() (if Penguin doesn’t override eat) 
int main() { 
    Penguin penguin; 
    Animal* animalPtr = &penguin; 
    std::cout << "Animal type: " << animalPtr->type << std::endl;  
    animalPtr->move();  
    animalPtr->Animal::eat();  // Explicitly call Animal's eat()  
 
    Bird* birdPtr = &penguin; 
    std::cout << "Bird type: " << birdPtr->type << std::endl;  
    birdPtr->ﬂy();  
    birdPtr->Bird::eat();      // Explicitly call Bird's eat()  
    return 0; 
}

اﻟﺑرﻣﺟﯾﺔ أﻛﺛر ﺗوﺛﯾﻘﺎ ذاﺗﯾﺎ ، ﺣﯾث ﯾﻛون ﻧوع

• إﻧﮭﺎ ﺗﺳﺎﻋد ﻓﻲ ﻣﻧﻊ اﻷﺧطﺎء ﻋن طرﯾﻖ ﺗوﺿﯾﺢ

• ﯾﻣﻛن أن ﺗؤدي اﻟﻛﺗﺎﺑﺔ اﻟﻣﺳﺗﻧﺑطﺔ) ﻋﻠﻰ ﺳﺑﯾل

اﻟﻘراءة ﻋن طرﯾﻖ ﺗﻘﻠﯾل اﻟﺗﻛرار ﻣﻊ اﻟﺣﻔﺎظ 
ﻋﻠﻰ ﺳﻼﻣﺔ اﻟﻛﺗﺎﺑﺔ. How do type declaration statements for 
simple variables affect the readability of a 
language, considering that some languages 
do not require them?  
Answer:  
Positive Impact on Readability : 
• Explicit type declarations make the 
code more self -documenting, as the 
intended data type of a variable is clear.  
• They help prevent errors by making 
type mismatches obvious.  
• They improve maintainability, 
especially in large programs, by 
reducing ambiguity.  
Negative Impact  : 
• They can add verbosity, making code 
longer and potentially harder to read if types are obvious from context (e.g., in Python: x = 5 vs. int x = 5 in Java)  .
 
• Inferred typing (e.g., in Haskell )  can 
improve readability by reducing 
redundancy while still maintaining 
type safety.

اﻟﺗﻲ ﺗﺗطﻠب ﻣﻌﺎﻟﺟﺔ ﻣﺑﺎﺷرة ﻟﻠذاﻛرة .
 اﻟﻌﯾوب :Some programming languages are typeless . 
What are the obvious advantages and disadvantages of having no types in a 
language?  
Answer:  
Advantages of Typeless Languages (e.g., 
assembly, BCPL, Forth):  
• Flexibility : Variables can hold any 
type of data, allowing for generic programming without explicit type constraints.  
• Simplicity : No need for complex type 
systems or type -checking 
mechanisms.  

 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ2  ﻣن7  Page 2 of 7  • اﻧﺧﻔﺎض اﻟﻣوﺛوﻗﯾﺔ: ﯾﺗم اﻛﺗﺷﺎف أﺧطﺎء ﻣﺛل 
ﻋدم ﺗطﺎﺑﻖ اﻟﻧوع أﺛﻧﺎء اﻟﺗﺷﻐﯾل ﺑدﻻً  ﻣن وﻗت 
اﻟﺗﺟﻣﯾﻊ .
• ﺿﻌف ﻗﺎﺑﻠﯾﺔ اﻟﻘراءة: ﺑدون إﻋﻼﻧﺎت اﻟﻧوع، 
ﺗﻛون ﻧﯾﺔ اﻟﻛود أﻗل وﺿوﺣًﺎ . 
• ﻋدم وﺟود ﻓﺣص ﻧوع ﻟﻠﻣﺗرﺟم:  أﻛﺛر ﻋرﺿﺔ  
ﻟﻸﺧطﺎء ﺑﺳﺑب اﻟﻌﻣﻠﯾﺎت ﻏﯾر اﻟﻣﻘﺻودة) ﻣﺛل 
إﺿﺎﻓﺔ  ﺳﻠﺳﻠﺔ ﻧﺻﯾﺔ إﻟﻰ ﻋدد  ﺻﺣﯾﺢ (.• Low -level Control : Useful for 
systems programming where direct 
memory manipulation is needed.  
Disadvantages : 
• Reduced Reliability : Errors like type 
mismatches are caught at runtime 
rather than compile time.  
• Poor Readability : Without type 
declarations, code intent is less clear.  
• No Compiler Type Checking : More 
prone to bugs due to unintended 
operations (e.g., adding a string to an integer).

اﻟﺳؤال اﻟراﺑﻊ 6 درﺟﺎت 6 Points  Question 4  
ﻣﺎ ھﻲ ﻛل اﻻﺧﺗﻼﻓﺎت ﺑﯾن أﻧواع ﺗﻌداد 
) Enumeration( ﻓﻲ ﻟﻐﺔ C ++   و Java؟ 
 What are all of  the differences between the 
enumeration types of C++ and those of Java?  
 
اﻹﺟﺎﺑﺔ: 
ﻓﯾﻣﺎ ﯾﻠﻲ اﻻﺧﺗﻼﻓﺎت ﺑﯾن أﻧواع اﻟﺗﻌداد ﻓﻲ  ﻟﻐﺗﻲ C++   و
Java: 
 
اﻟﺗﻣﺛﯾل اﻷﺳﺎﺳﻲ : 
ﻓﻲ C++، ﺗُطﺑّﻖ أﻧواع اﻟﺗﻌداد ﻛﻘﯾم ﻋدد  ﺻﺣﯾﺢ) int .(
أﻣﺎ ﻓﻲ Java، ﻓﮭﻲ ﻛﺎﺋﻧﺎت ﻣن ﻓﺋﺔ Enum . 
 
ﺳﻼﻣﺔ  اﻟﻧوع : 
ﺗُﻌدّ  أﻧواع Enum ﻓﻲ C++ ﺿﻌﯾﻔﺔ اﻟﻧوﻋﯾﺔ، ﺣﯾث ﯾُﻣﻛن  
ﺗﺣوﯾﻠﮭﺎ ﺿﻣﻧﯾًﺎ إﻟﻰ ﻋدد  ﺻﺣﯾﺢ   
) int x=Color::Red  .( 
ﻣن ﻧﺎﺣﯾﺔ أﺧرى، ﺗُﻌدّ  أﻧواع Enum ﻓﻲ Java ﻗوﯾﺔ  
اﻟﻧوﻋﯾﺔ وﺗﺳﺗﺧدم اﻟﻛﺎﺋﻧﺎت ﻟﺗﻣﺛﯾل اﻟﻌﻧﺎﺻر، وﻟذﻟك  ﻻ 
ﯾُﺳﻣﺢ ﺑﺎﻟﺗﺣوﯾل اﻟﺿﻣﻧﻲ .
 
اﻟطرق واﻟوظﺎﺋف اﻹﺿﺎﻓﯾﺔ : 
ﻻ ﯾُﻣﻛن ﻷﻧواع Enum ﻓﻲ C++ أن ﺗﺣﺗوي ﻋﻠﻰ طرق  
أو ﺣﻘول. وﻷن Java ﺗﺳﺗﺧدم ﻓﺋﺔ Enum وﻛﺎﺋﻧﺎﺗﮭﺎ  
ﻟﺗﻣﺛﯾل Enum، ﯾُﻣﻛن إﺿﺎﻓﺔ  اﻟطرق واﻟﺣﻘول. ﻋﻼوة  
ﻋﻠﻰ ذﻟك، ﺗﺳﻣﺢ Java ﻟـ Enum ﺑﺗﻧﻔﯾذ واﺟﮭﺎت  
(interface) واﺳﺗﺧدام طرق ﻣُﺟرّدة( Abstract 
methods). 
 
ﻣﺳﺎﺣﺔ اﻻﺳم  واﻟﻧطﺎق : 
ﺗُﺷوّه أﻧواع اﻟﺗﻌداد ﻓﻲ C++ ﻣﺳﺎﺣﺔ اﻻﺳم، ﻋﻠﻰ ﺳﺑﯾل  
اﻟﻣﺛﺎل :
enum Color { Red, Green, Blue } ; 
ﻻ ﯾُﻣﻛن ﺗﺳﻣﯾﺔ أي ﻣﺗﻐﯾرات Red أو Green  أو  
Blue، وﻋﺑﺎرة ﻣﺛل int Red=0 ;ﯾُﻧﺷﺊ ﺧطﺄً . ﻓﻲ ﺟﺎﻓﺎ،  
ﻷن ﻋﻧﺎﺻر اﻟﺗﻌداد ﻣُﻐﻠﱠﻔﺔ  داﺧل ﻓﺋﺔ اﻟﺗﻌداد، ﻓﺈن ﻧطﺎﻗﮭﺎ  
ﯾﻘﺗﺻر ﻋﻠﻰ اﻟﻔﺋﺔ . Answer:  
The following are the differences between 
Enumeration  types in C++ and Java:  
 
 
Underlying representation:  
In C++ Enum are implemented as int values. 
In Java they are objects of the class Enum.  
 
Type safety:   
C++ Enum are weakly typed as they can be 
implicitly converted  to int such as int 
x=Color::Red . Java on the other hand Enum 
are strong ly type d and use Objects to 
represent elements, therefore no implicit 
conversion is allowed.     
 
Methods & Additional Functionality:  
C++ Enum type cannot have methods or 
ﬁelds . Because Java uses Enum Class  and 
Objects for representing Enum eration, 
methods and ﬁelds can be added.  
Furthermore, Java permits Enum to 
implement interfaces and have abstract 
methods.   
 
Namespace & Scoping:  
C++ Enumeration pollute s the namespace , 
for example : 
enum Color { Red, Green, Blue };  
No variables can be named Red, Green or 
Blue and a statement such as int Red=0; 
generates an error. In java because the 
elements of an Enumeration are 
encapsulated within the Enum class the 
scope is limited to the class.

ﺑﺎﺳﺗﺧدام ﻣﺛﯾل ﻓﺋﺔ ﻓرﻋﯾﺔ أﯾﻧﻣﺎ ﯾُﺗوﻗﻊ وﺟود ﻓﺋﺔ أﺻﻠﯾﺔ . What exactly does it mean for a subclass to 
have an is -a relationship with  
its parent class?  
Answer:  
The  is-a relationship signiﬁes inheritance , 
where a subclass (derived class) is a 
specialized version of its parent class (base class).  This relationship enables 
polymorphism, allowing a subclass instance 
to be used wherever a parent class is 
expected.

ﺗﻌﻣل اﻟﻣﮭﻣﺔ A ﻛﺎﻣلﺎﻟﺑ ، ﺛم اﻟﻣﮭﻣﺔ B: 
 Suppose two tasks, A and B, must use the 
shared variable Buf_Size. Task 
A adds 2 to Buf_Size, and task B subtracts 1 
from it. Assume that such 
arithmetic operations are done by the three -
step process of fetching 
the current value, performing the arithmetic, 
and putting the new value 
back. In the absence of competition synchronization, what sequences of 
events are possible and what values result from these operations? Assume 
that the initial value of Buf_Size is 6.  
 Answer:  
Problem Statement summery :
 
• Shared Variable: Buf_Size (initial value 
= 6) . 
 
• Task A: Adds 2 to Buf_Size (performed as fetch → add → store)  .
 
 
• Task B: Subtracts 1 from Buf_Size (performed as fetch → subtract → store)  .
 
 
• No competition synchronization (no 
locks, atomic operations, or mutual 
exclusion).  
Possible Interleaving of Operations  : 
Since there is no synchronization, the operations of Task A and Task B can interleave arbitrarily. Below are some possible execution sequences and the resulting values of 
Buf_Size  :
 
Case 1: No Interleaving (Sequential 
Execution)  
 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ6  ﻣن7  Page 6 of 7  A :ﺟﻠب )6 ← (ﺟﻣﻊ (6+2=8)  ←ﺗﺧزﯾن )8 (

ﺣﺟم Buf_Size اﻟﻧﮭﺎﺋﻲ=  7 
 
ﺗﻌﻣل اﻟﻣﮭﻣﺔ B ،ﻛﺎﻣلﺎﻟﺑ ﺛم اﻟﻣﮭﻣﺔ A : 
 
B :ﺟﻠب) 6 ← (طرح (6-1=5)  ←ﺗﺧزﯾن) 5 ( 
A :ﺟﻠب) 5 ← (ﺟﻣﻊ (5+2=7)  ←ﺗﺧزﯾن) 7 ( 
ﺣﺟم Buf_Size اﻟﻧﮭﺎﺋﻲ=  7

 اﻟﺣﺎﻟﺔ 2 :ﺗداﺧل ﺟزﺋﻲ) ﺣﺎﻟﺔ ﺗﺳﺎﺑﻖ (

B ﯾﺟﻠب 6

B ﯾﺣﺳب 6-1=5 وﯾﺧزن 5 
A ﯾﺣﺳب  6+2=8 وﯾﺧزن 8  ) ﯾﺳﺗﺑدل ﺗﺣدﯾث B ( 
ﺣﺟم Buf اﻟﻧﮭﺎﺋﻲ=  8 )ﻏﯾر ﺻﺣﯾﺢ (
 
اﻟﻣﺛﺎل 3 :ﺗداﺧل  ﺻﺣﯾﺢ) اﻟﻧﮭﺎﺋﻲ=  7 ( 
A ﯾﺟﻠب 6 
A ﯾﺣﺳب 6+2=8 وﯾﺧزن 8 
B ﯾﺟﻠب 8 )ﺑﻌد أن ﯾﺧزن A ( 
B ﯾﺣﺳب 8-1=7  وﯾﺧزن 7 
ﺣﺟم Buf اﻟﻧﮭﺎﺋﻲ=  7 ) ﺻﺣﯾﺢ ( 
Task A runs fully, then Task B  : 
 
A: fetch (6) → add (6 + 2 = 8) → store  )8 ( 
B: fetch (8) → subtract (8 -  1 = 7) → store  )7 ( 
Final Buf_Size = 7  
 
Task B runs fully, then Task A  : 
 
B: fetch (6) → subtract (6 -  1 = 5) → store  )5 ( 
A: fetch (5) → add (5 + 2 = 7) → store  )7 ( 
Final Buf_Size = 7  
 If no interleaving occurs, the result is always 7  
 Case 2: Partial Interleaving (Race Condition)  
When Task A and Task B interleave at the fetch or store stages, incorrect results can occur due to lost updates.  
Example 1: Lost Update (Final = 5)  
A fetches 6  
B fetches 6 (before A stores)  
A computes 6 + 2 = 8 and stores 8  
B computes 6 -  1 = 5 and stores 5 (overwrites 
A’s update)  
Final Buf_Size = 5 (incorrect)  
 Example 2: Lost Update (Final = 8)  
B fetches 6  
A fetches 6 (before B stores)  
B computes 6 -  1 = 5 and stores 5  
A computes 6 + 2 = 8 and stores 8 (overwrites B’s update)  
Final Buf_Size = 8 (incorrect)  
 
Example 3: Correct Interleaving (Final = 7)  
A fetches 6  
A computes 6 + 2 = 8  
B fetches 8 (after A stores)  
B computes 8 -  1 = 7 and stores 7  
Final Buf_Size = 7 (correct)

 ﻣﺎ ﻋﻣل اﻟداﻟﺔ اﻟﺗﺎﻟﯾﺔ ﺑﻠﻐﺔ Schema؟ What does the following Scheme function 
do? 
(deﬁne (y s lis)  
   (cond  
      ((null? lis) '() )       ((equal? s (car lis)) lis)  
      (else (y s (cdr lis)))  
)) 
 ﺻﻔﺣﺔ7  ﻣن7  Page 7 of 7   
 
اﻹﺟﺎﺑﺔ :
 داﻟﺔ Sche me  اﻟﻣُﻌطﺎة ھﻲ داﻟﺔ ﺗﻛرارﯾﺔ ﺗُﺳﻣﻰ y، 
وﺗﺄﺧذ ﻣﻌﺎﻣﻠﯾن : 
 •s :ﻗﯾﻣﺔ ﻟﻠﺑﺣث .
 •lis :ﻗﺎﺋﻣﺔ  ﻟﻠﺑﺣث ﻓﯾﮭﺎ .
ﺗﺑﺣث اﻟداﻟﺔ  ﻋن  أول ظﮭور ﻟـ  s  ﻓﻲ lis، و : 
إذا وُﺟدت:  ﺗُرﺟﻊ اﻟﻘﺎﺋﻣﺔ اﻟﻔرﻋﯾﺔ  ﺑدءًا ﻣن أول ظﮭور ﻟـ   
s . 
إذا ﻟم ﺗُﻌﺛر ﻋﻠﯾﮭﺎ: ﺗُرﺟﻊ')( ) ﻗﺎﺋﻣﺔ ﻓﺎرﻏﺔ (. 
 
ﻣﺛﺎل :
) y 3 '(1 2 3 4 5 ((ﺗُرﺟﻊ) 3  4 5 (  
Answer:  
The given Scheme function is a recursive 
function named  y that takes two arguments:  
• s: A value to search for.  
• lis: A list to search in.  
The function searches for the ﬁrst occurrence 
of s in lis and  : 
If found: Returns the sublist starting at the 
ﬁrst occurrence of s .  
If not found: Returns '() (an empty list).  
Example  
(y 3 '(1 2 3 4 5))  returns  (3 4 5)

 ﻘﺎﺋﻣﺔﻟﻠﯾﺗم اﺣﺗﺳﺎب وﺟﻠب اﻟﻌﻧﺎﺻر اﻟﺧﻣس اﻷوﻟﻰ  
دون اﻟﺣﺎﺟﺔ اﻟﻰ اﺣﺗﺳﺎب ﺑﺎﻗﻲ ﻗﯾم اﻟﻘﺎﺋﻣﺔ. اﻟﻼﻧﮭﺎﺋﯾﺔ  What does lazy evaluation mean?  Give an 
example.  
Answer : 
Lazy Evaluation  is a strategy where an 
expression is not evaluated until its value 
is needed . It has the advantage of  
improv ing efficiency by avoiding 
unnecessary computations.  Lazy 
Evaluation also enables working with 
inﬁnite data structures (e.g., streams).  
 Example (in Haskell) : 
 
take 5 [1..]  
 
takes the ﬁrst 5 elements from an inﬁnite list without evaluating the entire list.
